---
title: "how to lock my user account?"
date: 2015-05-21
forum: Security
---

### Post by AkwatiKata on 2015-05-21
I have created a user account with a password. When I want to do some things, like updating Ubuntu, my password is required. I can also set it to require my password when the computer comes back from sleep mode. 
However, I cannot set it to require a password when logging in. There is a guest account, so when other people use this machine, they can use the Guest account, but if they want to use my account, they just click on it and no password is required.
How can I make it so that logging into my account requires my password just like in Windows? 
I don't know anything about command lines, so how can I do this through the 'normal' interface?

Thanks

---

### Post by Lars Noodén on 2015-05-21
It's there in a different place, under System Settings -> User Accounts -> your username -> Automatic Login -> Off

---

### Post by AkwatiKata on 2015-05-21
yes, I have tried that and turned automatic login off. So now when the machine starts, it gives a screen where I can see both my account and the Guest account. But when I click on my account, no password is required. I just click on it and it logs in

---

### Post by corti-nico on 2015-05-21
> **AkwatiKata said:**
> I have created a user account with a password. When I want to do some things, like updating Ubuntu, my password is required. I can also set it to require my password when the computer comes back from sleep mode. 
However, I cannot set it to require a password when logging in. There is a guest account, so when other people use this machine, they can use the Guest account, but if they want to use my account, they just click on it and no password is required.
How can I make it so that logging into my account requires my password just like in Windows? 
I don know anything about command lines, so how can I do this through the 'normal' interface?

Thanks

You can first try to disable guest login.
To do this just open file ```
/etc/lightdm/lightdm.conf
``` with this command:

```
sudo -H gedit /etc/lightdm/lightdm.conf
```

If file exists add the following line at the end:

```
allow-guest=false
```

If file does not exists please insert following rows:

```

[SeatDefaults]
user-session=ubuntu
greeter-session=unity-greeter 
allow-guest=false

```

Save and reboot your PC and let us know if Guest session. First do this and then will figure out why your password is not asked on login.

:p

### Post by deadflowr on 2015-05-21
What does the command 
```
id
```
say?

It is entirely possible that your user is in the nopasswdlogin group.
Users in this group can do as it suggests, login without a password.

Autologin, works different from what you describe.
In that autologin will login, without any user input.

Not sure if this what it is, but it's an idea...

---

### Post by steeldriver on 2015-05-21
^^^ THIS. nopasswdlogin is a separate mechanism from **auto**login (which doesn't even present the login screen)

---

### Post by steeldriver on 2015-05-21
AFAIK, the standard installation of Ubuntu doesn't use nopasswdlogin - it would have been something that the person installing it set up after

Regardless, you can remove a user  from the group simply using the command

```

sudo gpasswd --remove *username* nopasswdlogin

```

where *username* is replaced by the actual username you want to remove

---
